  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fa48f698-18fc-434f-8697-c102949fed40'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18365172252126723869">Monday 9th September<br/> ""I left London today and met Bingley at Netherfield Park. I had forgotten what good company he is; always ready to be pleased and always cheerful. After my difficult summer, it is good to be with him again. ...""<br/><br/>The only place Darcy could share his innermost feelings was in the private pages of his diary...<br/><br/>Torn between his sense of duty to his family </span>
  <span id="freeText18365172252126723869" style="display:none">Monday 9th September<br /> ""I left London today and met Bingley at Netherfield Park. I had forgotten what good company he is; always ready to be pleased and always cheerful. After my difficult summer, it is good to be with him again. ...""<br /><br />The only place Darcy could share his innermost feelings was in the private pages of his diary...<br /><br />Torn between his sense of duty to his family name and his growing passion for Elizabeth Bennet, all he can do is struggle not to fall in love.<br /><br />Mr. Darcy's Diary presents the story of the unlikely courtship of Elizabeth Bennet and Fitzwilliam Darcy from Darcy's point of view. This graceful imagining and sequel to Pride and Prejudice explains Darcy's moodiness and the difficulties of his reluctant relationship as he struggles to avoid falling in love with Miss Bennet. Though seemingly stiff and stubborn at times, Darcy's words prove him also to be quite devoted and endearing - qualities that eventually win over Miss Bennet's heart. This continuation of a classic romantic novel is charming and elegant, much like Darcy himself.<br /><br />Pride and Prejudice has inspired a large number of modern day sequels, the most successful of which focus on the rich, proud Mr. Darcy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18365172252126723869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/69675407-rivalic"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1518098992i/69675407._UX100_CR0,19,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/69675407-rivalic">Rivalic</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I totally get your question because I've had a few run ins with vulgar Darcy books. I can say with confidence that no, this book has nothing that woul<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I totally get your question because I've had a few run ins with vulgar Darcy books. I can say with confidence that no, this book has nothing that would make an 1800s lady blush. The author, Amanda Grange is very meticulous about keeping the book as close to the original source, "Pride and Prejudice" as possible. Jane Austen is my favorite author and when I first came upon all the continuing Darcy stories I found 90% of them were basically trashy romance novels, containing none of the original eloquence of P&amp;P. Honestly they should name them 50 Shades of Darcy they are that bad. Though I have found two authors that actucully write like the time period and have a story not just vulgar topics. Amanda Grange being the first with her Diary's of the mens point of view, and Marsha Altman who wrote over 12 books about the adventures of Darcy and Bingley's families. If you liked P&amp;P give Altman a try you won't be disappointed! <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=cotton-candy-fluff">cotton-candy-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=jane-austen-related">jane-austen-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=library-has">library-has</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604886945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15819718968772925689"><b>July</b><br/><br/>-Tried to find Georgiana a house in London<br/><br/>-Went to a dinner<br/><br/>-Went to another dinner<br/><br/>-Bingley said he wanted to rent an estate in the country. Pff! He'll be leaving it in a few weeks!<br/><br/>-Went to another dinner<br/><br/>-Decided to surprise Georgie in Ramsgate, but oh my gosh, <i>I</i> was the one who got surprised! And a terrible surprise at that. Wickham is on my black list forever. <br/><br/><b>August</b><br/><br/>-I did nothing interesting in August, but still wrote many entries.<br/><br/><b>September</b><br/><br/>-So, Bingley was serious about this estate-in-the-</span>
  <span id="freeText15819718968772925689" style="display:none"><b>July</b><br /><br />-Tried to find Georgiana a house in London<br /><br />-Went to a dinner<br /><br />-Went to another dinner<br /><br />-Bingley said he wanted to rent an estate in the country. Pff! He'll be leaving it in a few weeks!<br /><br />-Went to another dinner<br /><br />-Decided to surprise Georgie in Ramsgate, but oh my gosh, <i>I</i> was the one who got surprised! And a terrible surprise at that. Wickham is on my black list forever. <br /><br /><b>August</b><br /><br />-I did nothing interesting in August, but still wrote many entries.<br /><br /><b>September</b><br /><br />-So, Bingley was serious about this estate-in-the-country-thing, and I went with him to see Netherfield in Hertfordshire. <br /><br />-The neighbourhood sucks and the neighbours are tedious.<br /><br /><b>October</b><br /><br />-Went to the Meryton assembly and nearly died...OF BOREDOM!!<br /><br />-I hate the country.<br /><br />-Country folks are so...so...ARGH, so....I just can't even. I'm so above them, that I don't even know why I'm here!<br /><br />-Bingley got a new flirt. Wow, didn't take him long.<br /><br />-They almost made me dance with Elizabeth Bennet. *shudders* I'm so way too good for her. <br /><br /><b>November</b><br /><br />-Went to another horribly tedious party. UGH. THESE PEOPLE ARE SO BELOW ME!<br /><br />-That Lizzy Bennet is so smug. She's actually a little bit pretty though. Her eyes are quite fine. Actually, yeah, she's passably good-looking. <br /><br />-Her performance on the pianoforte is good though, let's all admit it. <br /><br />-She <i>is</i> intelligent.<br /><br />-And witty.<br /><br />-And...cute.<br /><br />-I stared at her the whole time today. <br /><br />-OH GOD SHE CAME TO NETHERFIELD!!!!<br /><br />-ELIZABEEETHHHHHHHHH!!!!<br /><br />-Bingley hosted a ball today and I DANCED WITH ELIZABETH!!!<br /><br />-Wait. WHAT THE HECK AM I DOING??! I can't be with Elizabeth!! I can't admire her! Her mother is a harpy, her youngest sister is a slut AND SHE HAS AN UNCLE IN CHEAPSIDE!!<br /><br />-Bingley, let's get out of here. NOW. Jane doesn't love you. Listen to me. WE NEED TO LEAVE.<br /><br /><b>December</b><br /><br />-Pheewwwwww crisis averted. Now let's forget Elizabeth Bennet. Should be easy-peasy-lemon-squeezy, because a man of my standing could never become allied to such a family as hers. <br /><br />-Is Bingley still thinking about Jane? No, right? I mean, she was just his flirt. She didn't expect anything from him. Why should she? WE ARE SO MUCH ABOVE THEM!!<br /><br />-Elizabeth.<br /><br />-Elizabeth.<br /><br />-Elizabeth.<br /><br /><b>January</b><br /><br />-What is Elizabeth doing.<br /><br /><b>February</b><br /><br />-Is Bingley still thinking about Jane? No, of course not. HE NEEDS TO FORGET HER, OKAY???<br /><br />-I miss Elizabeth's fine eyes.<br /><br /><b>April</b><br /><br />-ELIZABETH IS AT MY AUNT'S HOUSE!!!!!!!!<br /><br />-I totally lied, I HAVEN'T FORGOTTEN HER.<br /><br />-OOOOOOHHHH she looked at me today.<br /><br />-She must be SO happy to see me! ME! THE DARCY OF PEMBERLEY! Who wouldn't want me around?!<br /><br />-She's probably expecting my proposal. Probably has been expecting it for a loooonnggggg time. I WILL DO IT TODAY. I wonder how she'll say yes. <br /><br />-WWHHHAAAAAATTTTTT IN THE WORLD JUST HAPPENED????!!! SHE DARED TO REFUSE THE DARCY OF PEMBERLEY?! I don't get it. Her LOW connections. My AWESOMELY HIGH connections. Her STUPID family. My prestigious one. I LOVE HER AGAINST MY PRINCIPLES AND MY CHARACTER, AND EVEN TOLD HER AS MUCH, AND SHE REFUSES ME??!<br /><br />***<br /><br />OKAY, NO. I love Amanda Grange, and so far have enjoyed every book by her that I've read. I usually LOVE her take on Austen heroes. But THIS. WHAT WAS THIS???! Darcy was portrayed as the most pompous, vain, conceited being ever imagined. He was as bad as Mr. Collins! When he wasn't saying how much better he was than everyone else, he was either trying to convince himself that loving Elizabeth was a big no-no, or that Bingley and Jane could never happen. And when it wasn't that, it was listening to Caroline and not being annoyed by her, AND TELLING HIS COUSIN FITZWILLIAM THAT SHE WAS AN ADMIRABLE WOMAN HE SHOULD CONSIDER MARRYING. What on earth. <br /><br />It could have been amusing had it not also been tediously filled with pointless dinners and walks around parks, and if I hadn't set out reading this with the intention of falling for Mr. Darcy in the first place. This book gave me such a disgust of Darcy that I'm tempted to take back all I just wrote about him in my review of P&amp;P. NO MORE SWOONY. Do not talk to me of Darcy for now, or I shall say something I regret. <br /><br />I mean, Caroline Bingley a woman worth marrying his cousin? Granted, Caroline was hilarious in this book with her snarky little comments, BUT DARCY IS SUPPOSED TO DISLIKE HER. He didn't even see until almost the end that she was trying to win him and his Pemberley! Not only was he super arrogant and a major d*ck-head, but he couldn't even see what was going on under his very nose half the time. <br /><br />I'm sorry, but this book just did not work. It was boring, and Darcy was seen in a truly awful light. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15819718968772925689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14185150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12072100070218564622">Mildly entertaining to P&P fans in a couple of spots, but not really worth reading. I enjoyed one overheard conversation between Lady Catherine and Mr. Collins, and I enjoyed Col. Fitzwilliam's reaction when Darcy describes the manner in which he proposed to Elizabeth: essentially, "You said <i>what</i> to her?"<br/><br/>But the writing is terrible. Shallow, dull and repetitive - I hope I never see the word "satirically" again. It's not that great an adverb to begin with; why would you use it a dozen times in a </span>
  <span id="freeText12072100070218564622" style="display:none">Mildly entertaining to P&amp;P fans in a couple of spots, but not really worth reading. I enjoyed one overheard conversation between Lady Catherine and Mr. Collins, and I enjoyed Col. Fitzwilliam's reaction when Darcy describes the manner in which he proposed to Elizabeth: essentially, "You said <i>what</i> to her?"<br /><br />But the writing is terrible. Shallow, dull and repetitive - I hope I never see the word "satirically" again. It's not that great an adverb to begin with; why would you use it a dozen times in a short novel? And the author beats you over the head with recognizable phrases from P&amp;P.<br /><br />The diary framework was unrealistic and inconsistently crafted. Some entries were written as if Darcy were recalling the day's events, but others were written as if the action were happening real-time.<br /><br />I was annoyed that the author went to the trouble of making Lydia Bennet practically malicious, rather than only stupid and thoughtless.</span>

<div id="review_1929475823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1929475823" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1929475823?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1929475823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11614400866915484350">I've read this for one of my classes! (Which is actually a sort of Jane Austen and Charlotte Brontë fan club. Best class ever.)<br/><br/><b>“Elizabeth, Elizabeth, Elizabeth.”</b><br/><br/>Chances are, if Jane Austen is your goddess, you'll probably read this, reluctantly enjoy it, and wrinkle your nose at it afterwards, because of course nobody expects anyone to equal Jane Austen and, mathematically, every attempt to do so is bound to fail. I recommend to dive into the book light-heartedly and with light expectations. In </span>
  <span id="freeText11614400866915484350" style="display:none">I've read this for one of my classes! (Which is actually a sort of Jane Austen and Charlotte Brontë fan club. Best class ever.)<br /><br /><b>“Elizabeth, Elizabeth, Elizabeth.”</b><br /><br />Chances are, if Jane Austen is your goddess, you'll probably read this, reluctantly enjoy it, and wrinkle your nose at it afterwards, because of course nobody expects anyone to equal Jane Austen and, mathematically, every attempt to do so is bound to fail. I recommend to dive into the book light-heartedly and with light expectations. In doing so I was indeed able to find it quite entertaining; there's no comparing it to the original, but that is something I don't even need to spell out for you. <i>Mr. Darcy's Diary</i> is <b>an innocent retelling</b> that does no harm, though it's just as true that it could have done so much more good.<br /><br />•<b>My first complaint concerns the format</b>. The fact that the book is written as a diary only accomplished the task of making me wonder time and again <i>who</i> on earth would ever copy in his diary a letter he's about to send to a woman commenting on every single paragraph with such abundance of details, and <i>then</i> have the audacity to go to bed saying he's too tired to neatly write a fair copy. (My friend Chiara, who attends the aforementioned class with me, just read what I wrote over my shoulder and gave her approval.) It's just, <b>it killed my suspension of disbelief</b>. I think no one would ever keep a diary this way. <br /><br />•The other thing that in my opinion left a lot to be desired is <b>the characterization</b>. If there was one truly interesting thing about <b>re-writing <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> from Darcy's POV</b>, it was the opportunity to dig deeper into the feelings that accompanied him throughout his growth as a person (why, I think that was <i>entirely</i> the point, wasn't it?), but I think Grange didn't portray (let alone truly convey) Darcy's development and crucial change of mind well enough. Basically, right before leaving Rosings he writes to Elizabeth that arrogant letter we all know, then, when he's with Bingley and Caroline again, he hears her speak ill of Elizabeth and her family, he gets kind of mad, he changes his mind. That's it. His transformation felt too sudden, and even though it's obvious that he was being a presumptuous ass, not adequately motivated. (Though it was so satisfying to have him admit he had been and still was inconsistent with himself. Chiara's contribution again here.) <br /><br />•This is rather unimportant compared to my other points, but Elizabeth was a completely secondary character. Again, I ascribe it to the drawbacks of the diaristic form, and there's not really anything to be done about it.<br /><br />➽ All in all, I must say it was unexpectedly enjoyable, even if only for <b>allowing me to re-experience the favourite moments of one of my all-time favourite novels</b>. I think I'll also try out some of the other books in the Jane Austen Heroes series -I'm especially curious about Wentworth's and Knightley's. Also Edmund's doesn't sound bad at all, though...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11614400866915484350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27978204" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27978204" />
    <a title="M—" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1353617-m"><img alt="M—" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216772420p2/1353617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27978204?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M—" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M—" href="/user/show/1353617-m">M—</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1353617-m?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27978204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10178888904758156122">My Dear Readers, <br/><br/>It is with grave misfortune that I dissuade you from whatever excitement you may have upon learning of the existence of this novel. Jane Austen, the wonderful authoress that she is, has created such a wealth of characters and a story so beloved that more modern writers cannot help but continue to revisit the story and attempt to interpret it in a new way, but to no avail. <br/><br/><i>Mr. Darcy's Diary</i> is a straight retelling of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice' title='Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pride and Prejudice</a>, even directly quoting the original during </span>
  <span id="freeText10178888904758156122" style="display:none">My Dear Readers, <br /><br />It is with grave misfortune that I dissuade you from whatever excitement you may have upon learning of the existence of this novel. Jane Austen, the wonderful authoress that she is, has created such a wealth of characters and a story so beloved that more modern writers cannot help but continue to revisit the story and attempt to interpret it in a new way, but to no avail. <br /><br /><i>Mr. Darcy's Diary</i> is a straight retelling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a>, even directly quoting the original during key points in the plot. Grange has done a very admirable job of spinning the story from Darcy's point of view, but she hasn't been able to do it in an interesting or original way. Her efforts to recreate Darcy's formal and reserved personality within this diary-as-a-novel format have resulted in a very bland and wooden book where every twist of the story is predictable. Please take my assurance that it would be much more entertaining to reread Austen's original yet again. <br /><br />In short, Grange's rendition of Mr. Darcy's side of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> never inflamed my passions. And for all its formality in tone, the book is so familiar that it can only cause a brief entertainment. I'd recommend this book only to particular friends of the original story. <br /><br />Kindest regards, <br /><br />An Opinionated Lady</span>
  <a data-text-id="10178888904758156122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_498278503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/498278503" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10827825-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571182054p2/10827825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/498278503?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/10827825-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10827825-sharon?shelf=reviewed-2015">reviewed-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer498278503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6040481949140492032">If there was ever a "he said" book that you should read then this is it. Fans of Jane Austen's timeless classic will fall in love with Darcy all over again when they read the inner most thoughts of a man whom the world sees as proud and self-righteous.<br/><br/>Amanda Grange stays as close to Pride and Prejudice as possible in her re-telling of the timeless classic. There are enough similarities that I believe even Jane Austen herself would happily add this book to her collection. I have read quite a few </span>
  <span id="freeText6040481949140492032" style="display:none">If there was ever a "he said" book that you should read then this is it. Fans of Jane Austen's timeless classic will fall in love with Darcy all over again when they read the inner most thoughts of a man whom the world sees as proud and self-righteous.<br /><br />Amanda Grange stays as close to Pride and Prejudice as possible in her re-telling of the timeless classic. There are enough similarities that I believe even Jane Austen herself would happily add this book to her collection. I have read quite a few reviews that state this is nothing like the original and I think they have missed the whole point of the book. It is not meant to be like the original or is it trying to be. What this book gives us is an insight into Mr. Darcy, a deeper look at a man that has captured the hearts and minds of millions worldwide. I have had this book in my collection for quite a few years. I kept putting off reading it as I did not want to be disappointed if it fell short of the image of what kind of man I believe Mr. Darcy to be. It did not disappoint, in fact, it excelled all expectations. <br /><br />Although the book is written in diary form, you can easily connect to the characters. It is a delight to read exactly what Mr. Darcy thinks of all of the people in his acquaintance. From the carefree and friendly manner of Mr. Bingley to the ridiculous and improper Bennet family. There is nothing about this book that I can fault and I hope that fans of Jane Austen will find as much pleasure in reading it as I have found.<br /><br />Highly recommended reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6040481949140492032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3189718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3189718" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/141804-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262373695p2/141804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3189718?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/141804-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/141804-ashley?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/141804-ashley?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/141804-ashley?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/141804-ashley?shelf=regency">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3189718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3598770681588155000">After reading Pamela Aiden's "Fitzwilliam Darcy, Gentleman" trilogy a few months ago, I found this to be merely a much simpler version. Grange doesn't go much beyond the events we already know of from the original novel, and Darcy himself doesn't seem to have much depth at all. He switches from being determined to stop thinking about Elizabeth to suddenly proposing without almost any explanation at all. His feelings seem to flip flop to quickly throughout the novel with no basis. Overall, I knew</span>
  <span id="freeText3598770681588155000" style="display:none">After reading Pamela Aiden's "Fitzwilliam Darcy, Gentleman" trilogy a few months ago, I found this to be merely a much simpler version. Grange doesn't go much beyond the events we already know of from the original novel, and Darcy himself doesn't seem to have much depth at all. He switches from being determined to stop thinking about Elizabeth to suddenly proposing without almost any explanation at all. His feelings seem to flip flop to quickly throughout the novel with no basis. Overall, I knew exactly what was going to happen - there were no surprises. Nothing happens to Darcy that we don't already know about to some degree.<br />The book was enjoyable for the story itself, and of course I found myself smiling when Elizabeth finally accepted. The glimpses of their life after marriage were cute too. If you really want an in-depth look at Darcy, I recommend the Pamela Aiden trilogy. Although it can be a little far-fetched a times, she adds a slew of new characters for Darcy to interact with, and really shows the way his mind works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3598770681588155000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15441452297166384143">Nothing spectacular, just a retelling of Jane Austen's P&P from Mr. Darcy's perspective (his diary). <br/><br/>There's a lot of:<br/><i>I will pay Elizabeth no more attention.</i><br/>(You do that. I will enjoy seeing you try.)<br/><i>I did not miss Elizabeth at all. I believe I scarcely thought of her half a dozen times all day.</i><br/>(Should I count that as progress? Honestly...)<br/><i>I am not used to being so confused. I never was, before I met Elizabeth.</i><br/>(You are so doomed.)<br/><br/>There's also some of the following:<br/><i>I am looking forward to this ev</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15441452297166384143" style="display:none">Nothing spectacular, just a retelling of Jane Austen's P&amp;P from Mr. Darcy's perspective (his diary). <br /><br />There's a lot of:<br /><i>I will pay Elizabeth no more attention.</i><br />(You do that. I will enjoy seeing you try.)<br /><i>I did not miss Elizabeth at all. I believe I scarcely thought of her half a dozen times all day.</i><br />(Should I count that as progress? Honestly...)<br /><i>I am not used to being so confused. I never was, before I met Elizabeth.</i><br />(You are so doomed.)<br /><br />There's also some of the following:<br /><i>I am looking forward to this evening. After dinner, our true marriage will begin.</i><br />(Darcy, you dawg.)<br /><br />Like I said, there's nothing spectacular or groundbreaking about this book. It's quick. It's easy. It's relatively fun. So there's that. </span>

<div id="review_407978786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407978786" />
    <a title="Rebecca May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11349024-rebecca-may"><img alt="Rebecca May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531472983p2/11349024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407978786?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca May" href="/user/show/11349024-rebecca-may">Rebecca May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11349024-rebecca-may?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407978786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11550307592226779999">As with most of Amanda Grange’s Diary’s, I was absolutely, absolutely delighted with <i>Mr Darcy’s Diary</i>. Though I wouldn’t call it better than the original (as unfortunately I have had to say with others of the Diaries), it was certainly amazing, and definitely as good.<br/><br/>Again, I think part of the brilliance of this Diary can be attributed to the fact that the backstory from <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> is pretty well known – Amanda Grange wouldn’t have had to make many events up. That being said, the fact d</span>
  <span id="freeText11550307592226779999" style="display:none">As with most of Amanda Grange’s Diary’s, I was absolutely, absolutely delighted with <i>Mr Darcy’s Diary</i>. Though I wouldn’t call it better than the original (as unfortunately I have had to say with others of the Diaries), it was certainly amazing, and definitely as good.<br /><br />Again, I think part of the brilliance of this Diary can be attributed to the fact that the backstory from <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> is pretty well known – Amanda Grange wouldn’t have had to make many events up. That being said, the fact doesn’t detract from the quality of the Diary at all.<br /><br />Mr Darcy is well known to be – at least to begin with – the snootiest, most aloof of Jane Austen’s heroes. None of the others have his reputation for being immediately disliked by the heroine – except perhaps Colonel Brandon, but he was more ignored rather than disliked, and through no fault of his own. In any case, this Diary was a beautiful read, but more importantly it was <i>fun</i>. Probably more fun than any other of Amanda Grange’s Diaries that I have read so far. This is because we get to see the reasons and the man behind the snootiness.<br /><br />As we all know, Elizabeth Bennet’s wit and vivacity have been entertaining Jane Austen readers for years. And now I discover that her wit and vivacity entertained Mr Darcy just as much… along with irritating him immensely, confusing him, and drawing his attention to her “fine eyes”. Behind the cool exterior we see how much he enjoys the verbal sword-play, so different to the flattering, fawning annoyance he is usually subjected to by Miss Bingley.<br /><br />That is another thing that is amazing about <i>Mr Darcy’s Diary</i>; his slow realization that being well-bred with good connections does not mean you are a good person, and vice versa. He realizes that while Ms Bingley is “civilised” or “well-bred” – whatever you want to call it – that she lacks sincerity is cunning and scheming rather than intelligent. Furthermore he is ashamed to realize that his own aunt, despite being of a very high station, does not have the basic courtesy to be polite to guests in her own home. <br /><br />I also found it quite fun to get to know Colonel Fitzwilliam a bit better through the Diary, and witness Darcy’s horror as he realizes how Elizabeth found out about his interference in Jane’s affairs. We see that Mr Darcy is not uncaring – far from it – but simply has a set of very strict rules and values that he has gained through his sheltered upbringing.<br /><br />However, the Diary starts at the point when Darcy’s sheltered upbringing ends – with Wickham trying to steal away Georgiana. This is an incredibly touching beginning to the book. Mr Darcy’s righteous anger on behalf of his sister is sweet, as is her loyalty to him. But Wickham is such a bastard. While in <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> you had time to be wooed by Wickham’s easy manners, here you are plunged right into the truth of what an awful, insolent rogue he is. Not only when he attempts to elope with Georgiana, but when he has the nerve to kiss and caress Lydia in front of Darcy right after he finished admitting to Darcy that he didn’t really care for her at all. Oooh, I want to slap him. So bad.<br /><br />Darcy, for the rest of the Diary, goes through an extremely bad case of what I’m beginning to think of calling <i>Grangeitis</i>; of course, he is totally in love, and has no idea of it, even while admiring Elizabeth’s fine eyes and wit, despite her lack of suitable family and fortune. Here’s my abridged version of his thought progression throughout <i>Mr Darcy’s Diary</i>;<br /><br /><i>Netherfield: </i>”Nah, she’s not pretty enough for me. Wait, actually, I quite like those eyes… No, I shouldn’t associate with people like her… She looks remarkably pretty after that walk. What do you mean her hem was dirty? Never mind… Damn I love her conversation. Right, enough, I gotta go, I’m sure I’ll forget about her soon enough. Oh, and, by the way, Bingley, her sister isn’t good enough for you." <br /><br /><i>Rosings: </i>"Ooooh, look, there she is again! I don’t care, I don’t care, I don’t care… Wait on? How did I get in this room? I’m proposing? Hold on, take a step back here – I thought I didn’t love her? Dammit, I’m so confused. Whatever, I’m sure she’ll accept me. Ah crap, she knows about Jane. WHAT? SHE SAID NO? But I'm perfect, and a perfect gentleman, of course. What a bitch. That’s OK, I’ll write her an awesome letter and it’ll all be fine.”<br /><br /><i>Pemberley: </i>"Oh, woe is me! I’ve lost her. Dammit, why does she keep turning up? Must be nicer, Must be nicer, Must be nicer, Must be nicer, Must be nicer, Must be nicer…. Hey, she actually has some cool relatives! Hmm, I would never have guessed. Hey, Georgiana, come meet this young lady who refuses to marry me, I’m sure you’ll like her. WOAH, Elizabeth, why are you upset? Oooooooohhhhhhhhhhhh… jees, Wickham, stay out of my life! Hold on a moment, I can fix this, I don’t want Elizabeth unhappy. Off I go." *skips off*<br /><br /><i>London: </i>"Screw you, Wickham. Yes, OK, we might end up as brothers, and I’m giving you money, but screw you anyway. Oh, by the way, don’t tell Elizabeth."<br /><br /><i>Netherfield/Longbourn: </i>"Dammit, I was wrong. Bingley, you can totally marry Jane now, I was just kidding before. No, seriously. Besides, I want to see Elizabeth again. WHY ARE YOU IGNORING ME ELIZABETH! :’( She hates me. Oooh, hey Aunt, what are you doing here? Wait, she didn’t promise to not marry me?! Let me work that one through, there are too many double negatives here… Oooh, *happy face* Bye bye, Auntie, I’m off to propose to Elizabeth."<br /><br /><i>Netherfield: </i>"Yippie! She said yes! No, don’t tell me what a twit I used to be, Elizabeth, I don’t want to hear. Heehee, her parents are so confused. Ah, well." *extremely happy face*<br /><br /><i>Pemberley: </i>"PWND, Caroline. Being married to Elizabeth is awesome. I get to sleep with her now too. Oh, and by the way, Georgiana, have you ever thought about getting together with Colonel Fitzwilliam? I love being married! I love Elizabeth! I love my life!"<br /><br /><i>P.S: </i>"Screw you Wickham. You aren’t coming to my house, even if we are brothers. <b>EVER.</b>"<br /><br />So yeah, that should pretty much sum up my view of Amanda Grange’s adaptation of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, <i>Mr Darcy’s Diary</i>. Vastly entertaining, beautiful, amazing, and perfectly capturing the essence of Mr Darcy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11550307592226779999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3663568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8758554954119238972"> I know not everyone loves P&P the way I do, but the author follows the encouters between Darcy and Elizabeth authentically, keeping many aspects of the original in tack. It makes the book so wonderful, and because it's from Darcy's perspective so the author adds wonderful scenes like the discovery of Wickham in Ramsgate, Lady Catherine's diatribe to Darcy after speaking with Elizabeth, and some very satisfying scenes that round out Austin's original epilogue. <br/> The novel is written in modern Eng</span>
  <span id="freeText8758554954119238972" style="display:none"> I know not everyone loves P&amp;P the way I do, but the author follows the encouters between Darcy and Elizabeth authentically, keeping many aspects of the original in tack. It makes the book so wonderful, and because it's from Darcy's perspective so the author adds wonderful scenes like the discovery of Wickham in Ramsgate, Lady Catherine's diatribe to Darcy after speaking with Elizabeth, and some very satisfying scenes that round out Austin's original epilogue. <br /> The novel is written in modern English making it a quicker read than the original P&amp;P, but she keeps enough phrasing from the original to appeal to Austen fans. </span>

<div id="review_2328364733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328364733" />
    <a title="Zain Otoom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom"><img alt="Zain Otoom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598878687p2/45136398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328364733?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zain Otoom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zain Otoom" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom">Zain Otoom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328364733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12874259981027778591">Not bad at all! I was pleasantly surprised! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18351051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18351051" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/773197-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596061503p2/773197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18351051?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/773197-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/773197-katie?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18351051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17902431275966995889">I loved this book, almost as much as I love Pride & Prejudice, which says a lot because it is my favorite. I read this book in less than 24 hours! I have read many, many books by authors attempting to recreate Jane Austen's style and write sequels to continue her beloved stories, and they are never successful and I am always thoroughly disappointed. This one, however, was the closest anybody has ever come. It's Pride & Prejudice from Mr. Darcy's point of view. And anybody who has ever read and l</span>
  <span id="freeText17902431275966995889" style="display:none">I loved this book, almost as much as I love Pride &amp; Prejudice, which says a lot because it is my favorite. I read this book in less than 24 hours! I have read many, many books by authors attempting to recreate Jane Austen's style and write sequels to continue her beloved stories, and they are never successful and I am always thoroughly disappointed. This one, however, was the closest anybody has ever come. It's Pride &amp; Prejudice from Mr. Darcy's point of view. And anybody who has ever read and loved P&amp;P will certainly have wondered many times over just what he was thinking throughout the course of the story. With "Mr. Darcy's Diary," now you know. The author stayed very, very true to the original story, often times quoting it exactly. It was quite amusing to read what Mr. Darcy's impression was of the situations and conversations we have always heard described from Elizabeth Bennet's viewpoint. It was highly enlightening and I really feel the author got it exactly right. It was nice also that she did extend the story slightly to include several months after their wedding, a time which all P&amp;P fans have always wondered about and no author until now has ever adequately captured, in my opinion. She got it just right, and I was very satisfied with this book. That's why I will soon be reading a trilogy with the same premise, written by Pamela Aidan. I have read several reviews on Goodreads that indicate the trilogy is a more in-depth version of "Mr. Darcy's Diary" and very good as well. I recommend this book to all Jane Austen fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17902431275966995889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_816480831" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816480831" />
    <a title="Laurel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1406509-laurel"><img alt="Laurel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568061064p2/1406509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816480831?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel" href="/user/show/1406509-laurel">Laurel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=austen-sequel">austen-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1406509-laurel?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816480831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer345924396257117339">In 2005 author Amanda Grange gave <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> fans what they had been craving for centuries—Jane Austen’s classic story retold entirely from the perspective of its iconic romantic hero—Mr. Darcy. It was certainly not the first novel to explore this concept, but <i>Mr. Darcy’s Diary</i> remains, after many other attempts, the best in a very crowded field of Darcyiana.<br/><br/>I first read <i>Mr. Darcy’s Diary</i> eight years ago when it was released in the UK. I paid a fortune for the first edition to be shippe</span>
  <span id="freeText345924396257117339" style="display:none">In 2005 author Amanda Grange gave <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> fans what they had been craving for centuries—Jane Austen’s classic story retold entirely from the perspective of its iconic romantic hero—Mr. Darcy. It was certainly not the first novel to explore this concept, but <i>Mr. Darcy’s Diary</i> remains, after many other attempts, the best in a very crowded field of Darcyiana.<br /><br />I first read <i>Mr. Darcy’s Diary</i> eight years ago when it was released in the UK. I paid a fortune for the first edition to be shipped to the US. I did not regret it. My copy retains its place of honor on my Austen sequel bookshelf, along with the five other novels in her Austen Hero Diaries Series that Grange has since produced. She has a large international following for her work which she has earned through honest homage and clever craftsmanship.<br /><br />Writing a first person narrative of a classic hero who is a bit of a prig in the original story has its challenges. In <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> the reader sympathizes with the heroine Elizabeth Bennet in her dislike of Mr. Darcy. We meet him and draw our conclusions of his personality from her perspective—he is a proud and disagreeable man—we see why she thinks so, but we do not know why.<br /><br />Seeing the same events unfold from his eyes does not absolve him of his bad behavior, but as the narrative progresses, we are more sympathetic to his reasons. As we discover his inner thoughts and outward actions, our second impressions countermand his arrogant noble mien: we learn details of his chance intervention of the elopement of his sixteen-year old sister Georgiana with his nemesis George Wickham; we see his management of his soft-hearted friend Charles Bingley and learn why he is guiding him by the manipulation of his confidence and Bingley’s sisters; we see his attraction to Elizabeth Bennet spark and grow from his original cool intolerance to his admiration of her “fine eyes” and saucy impertinence—and his puzzlement of her brusque behavior to him.<br /><br /><i>"‘Oh,’ she said, ‘I heard you before; but could not immediately determine what to say in reply. You wanted me, I know, to say “Yes,” that you might have the pleasure of despising my taste; but I always delight in overthrowing those kind of schemes. I have therefore made up my mind to tell you, that I do not want to dance a reel at all – and now despise me if you dare.'<br /><br />‘Did I really seem so perverse to her? I wondered. And yet I could not help smiling at her sally, and her bravery in uttering it.’"</i> p. 40<br /><br />Close readers of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> will recognize lines of Austen’s original dialogue (like Elizabeth’s speech to Darcy quoted above) interlaced with Grange’s new text. This ingenious co-mingling is seamless and we partake in many of the important passages where Darcy interacts with Elizabeth in the original novel, and then his private reaction. This works for this reader because Grange does not try to write like Austen in Elizabeth head, but as Grange in Darcy’s.<br /><br />For those who are a student of character (like our heroine Elizabeth) it is interesting to observe our hero Darcy’s view of events from a male perspective. The whole <i>Men are from Mars, Women are from Venus</i> theory plays out beautifully and Grange takes full advantage of the differences in the sexes and how they think and react to the same scene when Elizabeth arrives at the Netherfield Ball.<br /><br /><i>“I continued walking towards her. ‘I am glad to see you here. I hope you had a pleasant journey?’ I asked. ‘This time, I hope you did not have to walk!’<br /><br />‘No, I thank you,’ she said stiffly. ‘I came in a carriage.’<br /><br />I wondered if I had offended her. Perhaps she felt I had meant my remark as a slight on her family’s inability to keep horses purely for their carriage. I tried to repair the damage of my first remark.’”</i> p. 51<br /><br />Clueless! There is some hope of improvement. As Darcy’s admiration of Elizabeth grows, it begins to humble his pride. While he is in Kent visiting his aunt Lady Catherine de Bourgh, we begin to see the change as he reacts to Elizabeth’s explanation to Darcy’s cousin Colonel Fitzwilliam of his behavior when they first met at the Meryton Assembly.<br /><br /><i>“In her eyes, my refusal to dance became ridiculous, and I saw it so myself, for the first time. To stride about in all my pride, instead of enjoying myself as any well-regulated man would have done. Absurd! I would not ordinarily have tolerated any such teasing, and yet there was something in her manner that removed any sting, and instead made it a cause for laughter.”</i> p. 78<br /><br />Even though many will know the final outcome of the story, Grange keeps us in suspense by adding new scenes and inner thoughts that only Darcy would be privy too—and now we are too. What fan of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i>, and Mr. Darcy, could possibly resist reliving a cherished novel and walking a mile in his shiny, black Hessian boots? I couldn’t.<br /><br />Laurel Ann, Austenprose</span>
  <a data-text-id="345924396257117339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_539599473" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/539599473" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15728061-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356883342p2/15728061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/539599473?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/15728061-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15728061-emily?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer539599473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2454737062095398511">I wasn't sure what to expect when I picked up this book. I've seen a lot of both really positive and really negative reviews. I personally was very pleasantly surprised with it. As to whether someone will like it or not, I think it really boils down to your expectation. We all have our own opinions, ideas, and expectations for exactly who each character is, how they should act or not act, and what is an acceptable outcome for them. If the books lines up fairly well with your personal opinion of </span>
  <span id="freeText2454737062095398511" style="display:none">I wasn't sure what to expect when I picked up this book. I've seen a lot of both really positive and really negative reviews. I personally was very pleasantly surprised with it. As to whether someone will like it or not, I think it really boils down to your expectation. We all have our own opinions, ideas, and expectations for exactly who each character is, how they should act or not act, and what is an acceptable outcome for them. If the books lines up fairly well with your personal opinion of the characters, it will likely be enjoyable. But that's such an individual qualification that it's impossible to make a blanket statement on whether or not someone else will really enjoy it like you do.<br /><br />I personally really enjoyed this book. I loved getting some more insight into other characters and "watching" Pride and Prejudice from a different angle. For the most part, I thought the characters stayed true to my idea of who they are. The writing is definitely not Jane Austen, but then, it's not supposed to be. <br /><br />I enjoyed "getting to know" Mr. Darcy better. It was fascinating to see his character grow through the book and to see the life and energy that Elizabeth gave to his life. He stayed true to who I think he is - a gentleman raised and confined in a certain level of society that led to his pride, yet with a caring and tender nature for those close to him, someone who seems aloof but realizes the great need for laughter and fun to lighten one's life a little. I felt like he changed his opinions a little too suddenly to fit his character (he had several "lightbulb" moments) but it wasn't major enough to hurt my enjoyment. I felt that he mentioned Elizabeth a little too much perhaps in relation to his other activities, but then again, he is a man infatuated/in love. My least favorite part in the movie was his first proposal to Elizabeth. It goes into much more detail than either the book or the movies and frankly, I thought it was horrible. I know it's meant to be arrogant and proud, but I thought it was overdone here.<br /><br />Charles and Caroline Bingley fit my ideas of them almost exactly, with Caroline being a little more bitter and acidic than is evident in P&amp;P. Lady Catherine was all pomp and arrogance. Georgiana was a little more shy and timid than I imagine her to be, and the scene at the beginning was rather awkward and almost laughable to me. But her character really blossomed at the end. Wickham is just as base as ever, though I was a little surprised by how base and moral-less Lydia was shown to be. I had always seen her as more vain and naive. I was delighted to see more of Colonel Fitzwilliam as I dearly loved him in P&amp;P and was always wanting to know more about him. I was most surprised by Anne de Bourgh - her character turned out quite different than I ever imagined or is ever shown in the movies, but in the end I enjoyed seeing her in a different light. Overall, I loved the book and seeing a beloved story from a different angle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2454737062095398511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62294360" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62294360" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1536431-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328995673p2/1536431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62294360?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/1536431-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62294360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2806927369769983758">Oh, know. Oh, know. Oh, know. <br/>After reading this book, I've discovered a little known fact that I never wanted to know, gasp: Mr. Darcy was one boring dude. <br/><br/>Kill me now. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, this harsh reality makes perfect sense, I mean, look how Austen portrays him in Pride and Prejudice? He rarely speaks unless spoken too, he's horribly shy amongst strangers, and nobody interesting, except Bingley of course, can stand to be around him he's so haughty and full of himself. <br/><br/>I thought the concept of Mr</span>
  <span id="freeText2806927369769983758" style="display:none">Oh, know. Oh, know. Oh, know. <br />After reading this book, I've discovered a little known fact that I never wanted to know, gasp: Mr. Darcy was one boring dude. <br /><br />Kill me now. <br /><br />Unfortunately, this harsh reality makes perfect sense, I mean, look how Austen portrays him in Pride and Prejudice? He rarely speaks unless spoken too, he's horribly shy amongst strangers, and nobody interesting, except Bingley of course, can stand to be around him he's so haughty and full of himself. <br /><br />I thought the concept of Mr. Darcy having a diary had great potential. What little tidbits would we find out about, I wondered. Like, what was he doing before he met Elizabeth, how exactly did he fall in love with her, what were his experiences with his sister and Bingley, etc. Exciting stuff, right? Well, no. In truth, I found him completely uninteresting and dull for about the first half of the book, and then when he drove Bingley from Jane Bennet, I thought him just plain mean. When he does begin to see Elizabeth is a different light, I of course, liked it better. A few more details here and there helped it become interesting enough by the end, but by then I was almost mad. <br /><br />Is that the author's fault? Is it even possible to make the true Mr. Darcy of Austen's novel the dashing romantic hero of almost every females dreams? Do we have the mini-series to thank for our obsession? Many,many years ago, long before 1995, I did my senior thesis on Jane Austen, and more specifically, Pride and Prejudice and Emma. I read both books and remember thinking them okay, not my favorite novels at the time - I was very young, but I don't remember thinking one way or the other about Darcy. In fact, I probably thought very little about him at all. Because that's how he's written. Elizabeth is the hero of Pride and Prejudice. It is she we come to love and admire first and foremost. <br /><br />And then along came the mini-series and Colin Firth. Ah....sigh. That changed everything didn't it. Now we've come to expect more from the man than what was really there. We invent truth were none exists. We invent, feelings and emotion expressed. We invent the feelings we saw on Colin Firth's face when he looked at Elizabeth, the dimple in her chin, the curve of her shape. In essence, we brought the book to life perfectly. But real life is never perfect. Expectations are never met, there is always let down. Rarely are men capable of jumping on the same romantic plane as women, because seriously we as a sex always expect too much, don't we? <br /><br />That was my main problem with this book. Like all my relationships I probably expected too much. I'm afraid Mr. Darcy I might have to break up with you after all these years. <br /><br />Sigh... <br />Just kidding. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2806927369769983758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122920336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122920336" />
    <a title="Katya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4324634-katya"><img alt="Katya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122920336?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katya" href="/user/show/4324634-katya">Katya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Somebody who's finished everything on fanfiction.net</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer122920336&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122920336" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8452928129296590909">I wonder, sometimes, what is it about Jane Austen, and "Pride and Prejudice" in particular, that makes it such a favorite subject of fanfiction. I mean, I have heard of the awesome power of the BBC 1995 mini-series adaptation, but I've never really experienced it first hand. <br/><br/>"Mr. Darcy's Diary" is exactly this - fanfiction. Nothing more and nothing less, just like "Pride and Prejudice and Zombies" and "Sense and Sensibility and Sea Monsters". Plotwise, it offers little other than a recap of the </span>
  <span id="freeText8452928129296590909" style="display:none">I wonder, sometimes, what is it about Jane Austen, and "Pride and Prejudice" in particular, that makes it such a favorite subject of fanfiction. I mean, I have heard of the awesome power of the BBC 1995 mini-series adaptation, but I've never really experienced it first hand. <br /><br />"Mr. Darcy's Diary" is exactly this - fanfiction. Nothing more and nothing less, just like "Pride and Prejudice and Zombies" and "Sense and Sensibility and Sea Monsters". Plotwise, it offers little other than a recap of the original novel from Darcy's point of view, and the original scenes soon lose their charm when the reader is forced to deal with Amanda Grange's poor writing. <br /><br />The rest of the book is just "Pride and Prejudice" told by Darcy, which in itself offers little in view of the actual story. After all, why pick up a book called "Mr. Darcy's Diary" if you haven't read "Pride and Prejudice" first? The book adopts a style that offers tremendous opportunities for character development, but instead of seizing the opportunity, Grange copies whole dialogues, word by word, from the original text, and sprinkles in some observations which I really could have gone without. Oh, there are some gems here and there, but they are few and far in between. <br /><br />Character development is nul. In fact, Mr. Darcy, portrayed in this book, is as whiny and annoying as they come. Also, from the dialogue and style of the narration, it's quite obvious that the author hasn't done her homework. Flitzwilliam Darcy is a Regency gentleman, is he not? Wouldn't his diary contain accounts of more things than balls and his romantic torments? Politics, perhaps? I would have never adressed this point if it hadn't been for a passage in this book, where he makes a point to let the reader know that the invasions of the French hold no interest to him. He's too busy mooning over Elizabeth, who is in the next room, and whom he cannot join until the men finish their political chit-chat. <br /><br />Gee, how flattering it must be, to give a woman more importance than Napoleon's wars. Yet, while the political future of Europe is clearly too insignificant for him, lengthy conversations about women's clothing and sauces apparently merit a full, word-to-word account in his diary.<br /><br />I won't ask why people read fanfiction. But the only difference between Amanda Grange, Seth Grahame-Smith and Ben H. Winters and the rest of us aspiring authors on fanfiction.net is that Amanda Grange, Seth Grahame-Smith and Ben H. Winters get paid. So why not put an effort into writing their books intead of letting poor Jane do half the work? I certainly have read better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8452928129296590909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_47553370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47553370" />
    <a title="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews"><img alt="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504749496p2/2073558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47553370?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)" href="/user/show/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews">Meredith (Austenesque Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews?shelf=pride-and-prejudice">pride-and-prejudice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2073558-meredith-austenesque-reviews?shelf=jane-austen">jane-austen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47553370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3027699133273418020">This novel is a collection of diary entries that Mr. Darcy might wrote throughout the course of his relationship with Elizabeth Bennet. Readers who love Pride and Prejudice who fell in love with Mr. Darcy would love the opportunity to become better aquainted with him, his character, and his thoughts. <br/><br/>I enjoyed this very easy read a lot. I think some things could have been improved, but overall any fan of Pride and Prejudice would find it an enjoyable read. When you read Darcy's side of the story</span>
  <span id="freeText3027699133273418020" style="display:none">This novel is a collection of diary entries that Mr. Darcy might wrote throughout the course of his relationship with Elizabeth Bennet. Readers who love Pride and Prejudice who fell in love with Mr. Darcy would love the opportunity to become better aquainted with him, his character, and his thoughts. <br /><br />I enjoyed this very easy read a lot. I think some things could have been improved, but overall any fan of Pride and Prejudice would find it an enjoyable read. When you read Darcy's side of the story you begin to understand his actions better than before. You realize when he first started to love Elizabeth and admire him for putting up with characters like Caroline Bingley and George Wickhm with the grace and disposition that he did. It is nice to be inside his mind at every point of the story and see things he only sees. This book is not in the style of Jane Austen's writing although it does borrow a lot of text and conversations from Pride and Prejudice (some of it not so accurately. <br /><br />Two things I did not like about this book were that MR. Darcy only wrote in his diary when he had something to say about Elizabeth, and sometimes skipped weeks or months. I know that this is fictional but I would like to believe that a man as important as Mr. Darcy if he decided to keep a diary would write of other things besides Elizabeth Bennet. I know we as readers would not find it as interesting, though. I have read Mr. Knightley's Diary by the same author and he seemed to have more to write about then just Emma. The second thing was that the author painted Charles Bingley as a flirt who was in and out of love so quickly all the time. I know he does not have the character of Mr. Darcy or the passion, but this book made me dislike him because of his fickleness. <br /><br />Overall it was a fun and easy read, but if you are choosy or critical about Pride and Prejudice or Jane Austen Sequels I would hesitate and read a few more reviews before purchasing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3027699133273418020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1390267317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1390267317" />
    <a title="Sarah - Thornton&#39;s girl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39733859-sarah---thornton-s-girl"><img alt="Sarah - Thornton&#39;s girl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443053943p2/39733859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1390267317?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah - Thornton&#39;s girl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah - Thornton&#39;s girl" href="/user/show/39733859-sarah---thornton-s-girl">Sarah - Thornton&#39;s girl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39733859-sarah---thornton-s-girl?shelf=books-to-buy">books-to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1390267317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13449024311309959935">So this book could of taken me about a day to read but I decided to have some breaks and make it two. I was completely surprised with this book its entirely different from how I'd thought it be...firstly I expected it to be quite a hard book to read and get into but its the total opposite. Amanda Grange slowly draws you in from the beginning from her very own take and perspective of Darcy as if could get either Colin firth's voice in your head or Matthew Macfadyen which ever Darcy you prefer the</span>
  <span id="freeText13449024311309959935" style="display:none">So this book could of taken me about a day to read but I decided to have some breaks and make it two. I was completely surprised with this book its entirely different from how I'd thought it be...firstly I expected it to be quite a hard book to read and get into but its the total opposite. Amanda Grange slowly draws you in from the beginning from her very own take and perspective of Darcy as if could get either Colin firth's voice in your head or Matthew Macfadyen which ever Darcy you prefer there voice was stuck in my head the whole time reading this book which is brilliant. <br>It does take awhile before Darcy meets Elizabeth but that's how the original story goes anyways. But its so interesting hearing from his point of view what Elizabeth meant to him and how he first fell for her. I have always admired Darcy as one of my number one Jane Austen Hero's. I especially enjoyed Pemberly and after they were married to realize how strong his feelings where for Elizabeth. <br>The book is drawn out a little bit but its a really an easy read and you get what you expect from Darcy that Amanda Grange helps create for us by writing his diary.<br>I highly recommend this book to any Jane Austen Fan and especially if you are like me and think of Darcy as your Number one hero. <br><br> <br><br><span>[image error]</span> </span>
